   3. Taillights: Red lights at the rear for visibility at night.
   4. Turn signals: Amber in front, red in rear for indicating turns or lane changes.
   5. Brake lights: Red lights at the rear and above the rear window for indicating slowing or stopping.
   6. Fog lights: At the rear to improve visibility in foggy conditions.
   7. Reverse lights: White lights at the rear to indicate the vehicle is in reverse.

- Pulse green when charging, with segments indicating charge level
- Stay green when fully charged
- Turn off when the vehicle is locked

This image shows a section of a vehicle manual titled "Vehicle Overview". It contains information about various lighting features of a vehicle. The manual describes four types of lights:

1. Daytime running lights or parking lights (Item 8): These are lights at the front and sides of the vehicle that make it more visible to other drivers while driving or parked. The manual notes that daytime running lights are brighter than parking lights.

2. Guide lights (Item 9): These are lights at the front and rear of the vehicle that help the driver and passengers see the surroundings at night.

3. Hazard lights (Item 10): These are amber front and red rear turn signals that flash to alert other drivers of a hazard or emergency. The manual provides instructions on how to activate the hazard lights using a button on the overhead console, and includes a small diagram of this console.

4. Flood lights (Item 11): These are lights behind the side mirrors that allow for better visibility of the area in front of the vehicle when it's dark outside. The manual provides instructions on how to turn these lights on or off through the vehicle's menu system.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page is titled "Vehicle Overview" and contains information about three different features of the vehicle:

1. Entry lights (Item 6):
   - These are lights on the side mirrors that project the Rivian R1S Compass logo onto the ground when the vehicle is unlocked.
   - The entry lights can be set to turn on when the vehicle is unlocked, when unlocked from close proximity, or when approaching the vehicle with proximity unlocking enabled.

2. Hazard lights (Item 7):
   - These are amber front and red rear turn signals that flash to alert other drivers of a hazard or emergency.
   - There's a Hazard Lights button on the overhead console to activate these lights in case of emergency or malfunction.
   - A small diagram shows the location of this button on the overhead console.

3. Flood lights (Item 8):
   - These are lights behind the side mirrors that illuminate the area in front of the vehicle when it's dark outside.
   - They can be activated through the Camping menu or the Vehicle menu on the center display.
   - There are options to turn a flood light on or off.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle, detailing the power outlets available in the vehicle. Here's a breakdown of the information provided:

1. Power Outlets Overview:
   - 12V
   - 120V
   - USB-C
   - Wireless Charger

2. Notes:
   - USB-C outlets in the center console storage bin can charge and store data (e.g., security footage from Gear Guard). These ports support up to 60W from a single port, with a total maximum capacity of 67.5W for two ports.
   - USB-C outlets at the back of head restraints, below the rear display screen, and near rear outboard seat armrests are for charging only. They support up to 15W per port, with a total maximum capacity of 30W.
   - Availability of outlets may vary depending on the vehicle model.

3. Diagram:
   The image includes a wireframe diagram of the vehicle interior, showing the locations of various USB-C ports and power outlets throughout the vehicle.

The page is titled "Vehicle Overview" and contains important safety information and details about the vehicle's power outlets. Here's a breakdown of the key points:

1. DANGER section:
   - Warns that Rivian R1S-supplied accessories work best with the vehicle.
   - Cautions against leaving non-Rivian R1S devices plugged in and unattended due to fire risk.
   - Advises not to obstruct any outlets in use.

2. Power Outlet Information:
   - 120V outlets: Power is off by default and can be turned on from the Energy app on the center display.
   - 12V outlet: Power is off when the vehicle is not in use, but on when the vehicle is in use. 12V power can be extended by turning on the 120V outlets.

3. CAUTION section:
   - Don't use outlets for devices requiring over 1,500 W (1.5 kW) of power.
   - Don't use more than one high-powered device at a time on 120V outlets.
   - Leaving 120V outlets powered on reduces the vehicle's range, even if no devices are plugged in.
---
The page is titled "Vehicle Overview" and focuses on explaining the "Accessory Power" feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Accessory Power allows the vehicle to remain powered on even when the driver walks away, locks the car, or restarts it.

2. A visual indicator in the center of the status bar shows when this power is on.

3. Notes:
   - Using accessory power reduces the vehicle's range.
   - 12V and USB-C outlets, as well as the wireless charging pad, are always on when the vehicle is in use.
   - "Outlets" can be turned on to keep power on when away from the vehicle.

4. To send power to the 120V outlets and keep other power sources active:
   1. Choose "Energy" from the app tray at the bottom of the center display, then choose "Outlets".
   2. Set the timer.
   3. Choose "Turn On Outlets".

5. An additional note states that while the timer is active, the outlets automatically turn off if the battery range becomes very low.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on "Software Updates" for a Rivian R1S vehicle. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Vehicle Software Update:
   - Updates can be done via Wi-Fi or cellular connection
   - The vehicle notifies you when an update is available
   - Information provided includes version number and estimated time for the update

2. Update Installation Options:
   - Install Now
   - Schedule for Later
   - Not Now (to clear the message without installing)

3. When Scheduling for Later:
   - You can select an installation time
   - Option to set up auto-install for future updates
   - Can choose to only install at home

4. If auto-install is set up:
   - You can choose to install now, change the time, or accept the scheduled time

5. Notes:
   - Auto-install times may vary by a few minutes
   - The system allows at least 8 hours between download and installation

6. Accessing Software Settings:
   - Go to Settings > Vehicle > Updates on the center display
---
The page is titled "Vehicle Overview" and provides important information about updating the vehicle's software. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Important prerequisites before updating the software:
   - Battery should have at least 35 miles of range
   - Vehicle should be in Park
   - Not connected to a DC fast charger
   - Tire Change mode should be off
   - System temperatures should be normal
   - 12V battery should be charged and healthy
   - Pet Comfort should be off
   - Vehicle leveling should be off
   - All passengers should exit the vehicle (suggested)

2. If these requirements are not met when an update is available, you'll receive a notification with options to:
   - Go to Updates to learn more
   - Got It to close the notification

3. Caution:
   - Don't touch pedals or buttons during the update to avoid interrupting it and disabling the vehicle

4. Additional notes:
   - Storage access, locking, and security features are unavailable during updates
   - Check the center display for more information if the update doesn't complete

This page is from a vehicle user manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page is titled "Access and Safety" and focuses on "Driver Profile Settings". Here's a summary of the content:

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page is titled "Access and Safety" and focuses on "Vehicle Access" and "Keys". Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Vehicle Access:
   - Users can use a key card or phone key to lock and unlock the vehicle.
   - Proximity Lock and Unlock feature automatically locks/unlocks the vehicle when you're near it with a phone key.
   - Lock icons in the center display can be used to lock/unlock the vehicle or check lock status.
   - Locking behaviors can be set in Settings > Vehicle > Access.

2. Notes on Vehicle Access:
   - In Settings > Drivers and Keys, black dots identify the key that unlocked the vehicle and its owner.
   - Doors automatically lock when driving starts.
   - If a door isn't opened within 2 minutes of an unlock command, the vehicle relocks automatically.

3. Key Card:
   - To use the key card, touch it to the reader on the driver's door handle and wait a few seconds.

4. Notes on Key Card:
   - The key card only works on the driver door; passenger doors don't have card readers.
   - If the vehicle is asleep, touch the key card to the driver's door handle for up to 8 seconds.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on "Access and Safety" and "Theft Protection" features. The document is from Rivian R1S, as indicated by the logo at the bottom of the page.

The main content describes how the vehicle is equipped with an immobilizer to prevent theft. It includes a warning not to leave the vehicle unattended and unlocked with the key card or phone key inside.

The document then provides tables explaining how the immobilizer works in various entry and exit scenarios for both a Phone Key and a Key Card.

For the Phone Key, it describes:
1. Passive entry
2. Passive exit
3. Active exit

For the Key Card, it describes:
1. Active entry

Each scenario lists the requirements and the corresponding immobilizer status. For example, for passive entry with a phone key, the requirements are:
- Phone key is authenticated
- Driver is seated in the driver's seat
- Vehicle is in Park

The immobilizer status for this scenario is that the system turns off the immobilizer and the driver can operate the vehicle.

The document provides detailed information about how the system behaves in different situations, such as when the driver exits the vehicle or walks away with the authenticated phone key.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically detailing the "Access and Safety" features. The page is numbered 36 and contains a table with three main sections:

1. Enter or Exit
2. Requirements
3. Immobilizer Status

The table describes three scenarios:

1. Active exit
2. System times out with the driver in the driver's seat
3. System times out after the driver leaves the vehicle

For each scenario, it lists the requirements and the corresponding immobilizer status. The information primarily focuses on the use of an authenticated key card, the vehicle being in Park, and the driver's actions (such as exiting the vehicle or being seated).

Key points include:
- The immobilizer system is enabled when the driver exits with the authenticated key card.
- The system keeps the immobilizer enabled if the driver doesn't place the key card against the interior card reader when seated.
- The vehicle can't be driven until the driver returns with a key or places the key card against the interior card reader.

This manual page emphasizes the importance of the key card in the vehicle's security system and how it interacts with the immobilizer to prevent unauthorized use of the vehicle.

This page is from a vehicle user manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle, focusing on "Access and Safety" related to the doors. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Opening doors from the outside:
   - When you unlock the vehicle, exterior door handles present themselves.
   - Pull a handle to open a door.
   - An illustration shows the door handle and its movement.

2. Notes on exterior handles:
   - They retract and lock when you drive the vehicle.
   - In freezing conditions, handles may freeze. To unfreeze, press the rearward end repeatedly.
   - If a handle doesn't present, push the indentation at the back of the handle, then pull to open.

3. Opening doors from the inside:
   - Press the open door button to open the door.

4. Emergency situation:
   - If the vehicle loses power, manual releases can be used to open front or rear doors from inside.
   - An illustration shows the interior door panel with the manual release area.

This manual page provides important safety information for accessing and operating the vehicle's doors under various conditions.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically detailing the "Roomy Entry and Exit" feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. The feature allows the driver's seat and steering wheel to move automatically for easier access when entering and exiting the vehicle.

2. It's disabled by default and settings are saved to a specific user profile.

3. An important note mentions that the seat and steering wheel must be calibrated for this feature to work.

4. The manual provides step-by-step instructions to set up the feature:
   - Navigate to Settings > Vehicle > Access on the center display
   - Choose "Set Position" under Roomy entry and exit
   - Ensure nothing is behind the seat and select "Got It"
   - Adjust the steering wheel and seat to desired positions
   - Choose "Remember Position" to save the settings

5. A warning is included to prevent injury by ensuring no one is around the seat when setting positions.

6. A note explains how to stop the automatic movement if needed.

This page focuses on"Access and Safety" features. The page details the following information:

1. After setup completion, a toggle switch and buttons for Change Position and Forget Position appear.

2. A table describing four buttons and their functions:
   - Toggle switch: Enables or disables the roomy entry and exit position.
   - Change Position: Makes changes to saved steering wheel and seat positions.
   - Forget Position: Removes saved position and turns off roomy entry and exit. Requires setup again if forgotten.
   - Set Position: Sets up the roomy position for the first time or when no position is saved.

3. Notes section with two points:
   - The vehicle adjusts to your driving position when you enter and press the brake pedal.
   - Roomy entry and exit moves the seat to the entry/exit position when the driver unbuckles at the end of a drive.

   - Available on either or both rear vehicle doors

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on the topic of "Airbags" under the "Access and Safety" section. The content provides important information about the airbag system in the vehicle. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. About Airbags:
   - The vehicle is equipped with supplemental restraint system (SRS) airbags.
   - Airbags are designed to supplement the protection provided by seat belts.
   - The vehicle has airbags and shoulder and lap seat belts for driver and passengers.
   - Airbags are not a substitute for seat belts, and all occupants should wear seat belts.
   - Failure to use seat belts increases the risk of severe injury or death in a crash.

2. Airbag Maintenance:
   - Airbags don't require routine maintenance.
   - Modifications for people with disabilities may affect the advanced airbag system.

3. How Airbags Work:
   - Sensors predict crash severity and deploy restraints when a threshold is reached.
   - Airbags deploy instantly with a loud sound during significant vehicle deceleration.
   - Not all collisions deploy airbags (e.g., low severity and rear collisions).

4. Front Passenger Seat:
   - Has an Occupant Classification System to determine if the seat is occupied.
   - Can deactivate the airbag under certain conditions.

This page focuses on"Access and Safety" and detailing the "Occupancy Detection" system. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Occupant Classification System (OCS):
   - Properly classifies front seat occupants
   - Occupants must sit upright in the center of the seat, with back against the seat back and legs extended
   - Occupants should remain seated in this position for the entire trip

2. The OCS may not classify occupants correctly if they:
   - Don't sit upright
   - Lean against the door or center console
   - Sit toward the front edge of the seat
   - Put legs/feet on the dashboard
   - Pull the seatbelt out fully, activating the Automatic Locking Retractor (ALR)

3. If the Passenger Airbag Off indicator is on when an adult is in the seat:
   - Ensure the occupant sits properly
   - It takes about 8 seconds for the OCS to update
   - If still incorrect, move the passenger to the rear seats
   - Contact Rivian R1S for system check

4. Conditions that can interfere with OCS accuracy:
   - Objects under the seat
   - Heavy objects on the seat
   - Objects wedged in various parts of the seat
   - Heavy objects on the occupant's lap
   - Seat accessories like covers or massagers

5. If issues persist after addressing these conditions:
   - Move passengers to rear seats
   - Contact Rivian R1S for airbag system check

The document emphasizes the importance of proper seating for safety system effectiveness and provides troubleshooting steps for potential issues with the occupancy detection system.

   - Choose Edit next to Window Locks
   - Select windows to lock/unlock on the vehicle image
   - Choose Done

3. Indicators:
   - "ON: REAR" appears when rear windows are locked
   - "ON: ALL PASSENGER" shows when all windows are locked
   - "ON: CUSTOM" indicates when some windows are locked

4. To turn off window locking, choose Window Locks again

The manual also includes some important notes:
- Locking a passenger window disables the window switch on the passenger door but not on the driver's door
- Window Locks remembers the previous setting on vehicle start-up
- To clear custom settings, deselect all windows in the Edit Window Locks panel

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on tire quality grading and safety information. The page is titled "Access and Safety" and covers the topic of "Uniform Tire Quality Grading."

The content is divided into several sections:

1. Treadwear: Explains how treadwear grade is a comparative rating based on tire wear rate under controlled conditions.

2. Traction - AA, A, B, and C: Describes traction grades and their meaning, with AA being the highest and C potentially indicating poor traction performance.

3. Temperature - A, B, and C: Discusses temperature grades and their significance in relation to heat resistance and dissipation.

There are two warning boxes:

1. The first warns that the traction grade is based on straight-ahead braking tests and does not include cornering traction.

2. The second cautions that the temperature grade is for properly inflated and not overloaded tires, and that excessive speed, under-inflation, or overloading can cause heat buildup and possible tire failure.

The document also mentions that the grade C for temperature corresponds to the minimum performance level required for passenger car tires under Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard No. 109.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on "Access and Safety" with details about "Snow Traction Devices". The content provides information on appropriate snow traction devices for different tire sizes and includes several important cautions:

1. For 275/65R20 tires:
   - Only use government-approved textile-based snow traction devices
   - CAUTION: Don't use snow chains or cables as they can damage the vehicle body

2. For HL275/50R22 and 275/60R20 tires:
   - Use low profile (16 mm or smaller) snow cables
   - Install the low profile cables on the rear tires
   - Ensure the vehicle is in a four-wheel drive mode such as Snow mode

3. For HL305/45R22 tires:
   - CAUTION: Don't use snow socks, snow chains, or cables as they can damage the vehicle body

The manual also includes a general caution about summer tires, stating they are not recommended for use in winter conditions, with snow traction devices, or at temperatures below 40°F.

This page focusses on the Tire Pressure Monitoring System (TPMS). Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Tire Pressure Monitoring System:
   - The vehicle has a TPMS that displays individual tire pressure.
   - It shows a low tire pressure indicator if a tire is significantly under-inflated.
   - All tires, including the spare, should be checked monthly when cold.

2. Safety Feature:
   - The TPMS illuminates a telltale when one or more tires are significantly under-inflated.
   - Drivers should stop and check tires as soon as possible when this occurs.

3. Importance of Proper Inflation:
   - Under-inflated tires can overheat, leading to tire failure.
   - It also reduces fuel efficiency, tire tread life, and affects vehicle handling.

4. TPMS Malfunction Indicator:
   - Indicates when the system is not operating properly.
   - The indicator flashes for about a minute, then remains illuminated when malfunctioning.

5. TPMS Sensor Automatic Learning Process:
   - Sensors are in each wheel's valve stem.
   - The learning process takes less than 10 minutes when you start driving.

6. Spare Tire TPMS Sensor:
   - The full-size spare tire (if equipped) has a passive TPMS sensor.
   - It becomes active when installed as a driving wheel.

The document emphasizes that the TPMS is not a substitute for proper tire maintenance, and it's the driver's responsibility to maintain correct tire pressure. The manual page is from a Rivian R1S vehicle, as indicated by the Rivian R1S logo at the bottom.
---
This page focuses on"Access and Safety" related to tire pressure and the Tire Pressure Monitoring System (TPMS). Here's a summary of the key points:

1. The compact spare tire, if equipped, doesn't have a TPMS sensor and doesn't display tire pressure.

2. Notes:
   - Replace the valve stem cap to protect the TPMS sensor from dirt.
   - When the tire is warm, fill it to 4 psi (27 kPa) above the recommended cold tire pressure.
   - The vehicle may need to be driven for up to 10 minutes at over 18 mph (30 km/h) before displaying a pressure reading.

3. Danger warning:
   - An underinflated tire may fail, causing loss of vehicle control and potential injury or death.

4. Caution:
   - Don't use the TPMS as a pressure gauge when filling tires.
   - The TPMS isn't designed for aftermarket wheels.
   - Use the same tire size and style as provided by Rivian R1S when replacing tires.

The page is titled "Access and Safety" and provides instructions on how to remove and reinstall the aerodynamic wheel cover.

The content includes:

This page details the "Phone and Media" functions.

The main content of the page is a table that explains various phone-related icons and their functions. Here's a summary of the information provided:

1. Reject and Send to Voicemail: Rejects an incoming call and sends it to voicemail.
2. Hold and Accept: Puts the current call on hold and accepts an incoming call.
3. End and Accept: Ends the current call and accepts a second incoming call.
4. End Call on Hold and Accept: For when you have two active calls and an incoming call, it ends the call on hold and accepts the incoming call.
5. Mute: Mutes or unmutes your microphone.
6. Switch Calls: Allows switching between two active calls.
7. Merge: Merges more than one active call.
8. Keypad: Used to respond to automated phone systems.

The table also includes a NOTE section explaining how to make a call using the center display.

Below the table, there's a section titled "Make SOS or Emergency Calls" which briefly mentions that SOS or emergency calls don't require the phone to be paired with the vehicle via Bluetooth. It refers readers to "Emergency SOS" for more information.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically detailing the "Wireless Charger" feature under the "Phone and Media" section. Here are the key points:

1. The wireless charger is located on the upper tray of the center console and is compatible with Qi-enabled devices.

2. To charge, place the phone face-up on the charger, aligning it with the center rib of the charging pad.

3. Charging times vary but typically take 2 to 3 hours to fully charge a depleted phone.

4. The charger works with most standard phone cases.

5. It can charge two phones simultaneously but works best with one phone and a small item like earbuds.

6. The charging pad has a temperature sensor and will stop charging if it gets too hot.

7. A caution note warns against placing metallic or magnetic objects on the pad or between the phone and charger.

8. The pad is only meant for compatible devices with rechargeable batteries.

9. While key cards or credit cards won't be damaged by the pad, their presence will prevent charging.

This image shows a troubleshooting guide for phone and media devices, from a Rivian R1S vehicle manual. The guide is divided into two columns: "If This Happens" and "Try This".

The guide addresses three main issues:

1. Device is too hot
   - Solution: Remove the device from the charger, wait for it to cool down, and try charging again later.

2. Wireless charger sensor doesn't detect compatible device
   - Solutions:
     - Remove any wallet cases from the phone.
     - Remove phone cases thicker than 5 millimeters for best phone detection and charging performance.
     - Remove the device from the charger, wait a few seconds, and place it back on the pad.
     - Move the device to another position on the charger to find proper charging positioning.

3. Device won't charge
   - Solutions:
     - Ensure the device is a 1.2.4 qi-compatible device (such as iPhone® and Android™ mobile devices, or pair of earbuds).
     - Ensure you're logged into your account on the center display.
     - Place the phone face-up against the center rib of the charging pad.
     - Ensure there isn't an incompatible object on the charging pad (such as key cards, foreign objects, or metal pieces). Remove items like coins or credit cards from the storage pocket of a phone case.
     - Respond to any warning on the center display that indicates an unauthorized item on the charging pad.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically focusing on the "Phone and Media" settings. The page details several audio adjustment features available in the vehicle:

1. Change the Equalizer Settings: This allows users to adjust volume levels of frequency bands to fine-tune the sound. There's an option to reset all equalizer (EQ) controls to default settings (all values set to 0) using a Reset button. Users can also choose preset equalizer settings by selecting "More" and picking from available presets.

2. Change the Soundstage Center: For vehicles equipped with this setting, users can control where the audio focuses. There's also a Reset option to return to the default setting.

3. Change the 3D Surround Sound: This feature allows control over the depth of immersion experienced in the surround sound field by both driver and passengers.

4. Change the Dynamic Sound Adjustment: The sound system automatically adjusts volume based on the vehicle's speed to maintain consistent loudness. Available settings are Off, Low (default), and High.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on the "Brakes" section.Here's a summary of the key points covered:

1. Regenerative Braking:
   - Happens automatically when lifting foot off accelerator
   - Captures energy and increases range
   - Regenerative Braking Assist feature for smoother deceleration
   - Not available when towing a trailer

2. Regenerative Braking Settings:
   - Can be adjusted in Drive Modes > Brake Regen
   - Standard: Default for most modes
   - High: Stronger braking, faster slowdown, more energy capture
   - Low: Default for Snow and Soft Sand modes, limited regeneration

3. Brake Lights:
   - Automatically illuminate during regenerative braking

4. Notes on Regenerative Braking:
   - May be reduced when battery is cold, fully charged, or almost fully charged
   - Use brake pedal to slow or stop if needed

5. Anti-lock Braking System:
   - Prevents wheel lock-up during braking
   - Helps maintain control on slippery surfaces

6. Electronic Park Brake:
   - Engages when vehicle is put in Park
   - Keeps vehicle from rolling

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page is titled "Driving" and focuses on explaining the "Vehicle Hold" feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Vehicle Hold:
   - Stops and holds the vehicle stationary without pressing the brake pedal
   - A Hold icon appears on the driver display when active
   - If malfunctioning, an indicator appears at the bottom of the driver display

2. Automatic behavior:
   - If you take your foot off the accelerator without braking, the vehicle slows and stops after 10 minutes
   - It then shifts to Park and engages the electronic park brake
   - When active, the vehicle shifts to Park if you exit

3. Note: To release Vehicle Hold while in Neutral, press the brake pedal

4. Vehicle Hold Not Available:
   - A notification appears if the feature isn't available or can't engage on steep grades
   - In such cases, use the brake pedal to stop and shift to Park before exiting
   - Refers to Emergency Deceleration if normal braking doesn't work

5. Vehicle Hold Error:
   - If an error occurs while stationary, the vehicle automatically shifts to Park
   - If an error happens three consecutive times when trying to shift out of Park, Vehicle Hold is disabled
   - Instructs to contact Rivian R1S in this case

---
This page focuses onthe Electronic Stability Control (ESC) and Traction Control System (TCS). Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Electronic Stability Control (ESC):
   - Helps maintain vehicle control with the brake system
   - Provides anti-skid support, especially on low-grip surfaces
   - Helps prevent loss of vehicle control

2. Traction Control System (TCS):
   - Adjusts motor and brake output to optimize traction
   - Limits wheel slip or spin

3. Stability Settings:
   - Can be adjusted manually from Drive Modes on the center display
   - Affects both ESC and TCS

4. Important Notes:
   - ESC and TCS are set to On by default at the start of a trip
   - If set to Reduced or Off, they default back to On at vehicle restart
   - An indicator appears on the driver display when Stability is Reduced or Off

5. Warnings:
   - It's recommended to keep Stability on in most driving conditions
   - Turning off Stability disables both ESC and TCS
   - Disabling or reducing these systems may lead to loss of control or crashes in certain situations

The manual emphasizes the importance of these systems for safe driving and warns about the potential risks of disabling them. It also mentions that the vehicle may prompt the driver to confirm Stability mode upon leaving the vehicle.
---

This page is from a Rivian R1S vehicle manual, specifically detailing the different driving modes available for both on-road and off-road conditions. The page is titled "Driving".

The manual describes five different drive modes:

1. On-Road Drive Modes:
   - All-Purpose: Maximizes comfort for daily driving, recommended for all on-road conditions including rainy weather. It adjusts ride height based on speed for better aerodynamics and range.
   - Sport: Prioritizes vehicle performance and responsive driving, stiffens suspension, and maintains all-wheel drive for maximum power transfer.
   - Snow: Maximizes control on snowy, slushy, or icy roads with relaxed pedal response and reduced regenerative braking.

2. Off-Road Drive Modes:
   - All-Terrain: For moderate off-road conditions, increases ride height and softens suspension.
   - Soft Sand: Maximizes performance in deep sand using specific traction control settings and reduced regenerative braking.

Each mode is accompanied by an icon for easy identification. The manual also includes notes about customizing ride height settings and mentions that All-Purpose mode can switch to front-wheel drive in Dual-Motor vehicles to save energy.

There's a special note for snow conditions, advising to use All-Terrain mode when going off-road in snow.

The document provides hyperlinks for more information on topics like "Ride Height" and "off-road driving," suggesting this is likely part of a digital manual or has corresponding sections in a physical manual.

This page gives a comprehensive overview of how the Rivian R1S vehicle can be optimized for various driving conditions, showcasing its versatility for both on-road and off-road use.

This page focuses onthe "Stability" settings. The page explains how to choose a Stability setting based on the drive mode and provides details on three stability options:

1. On: Electronic Stability Control (ESC) and Traction Control System (TCS) provide maximum stability and traction in all driving conditions.

2. Reduced: Both ESC and TCS activate to help stabilize the vehicle, allowing a small amount of wheel spin.

3. Off: Completely disables ESC and keeps TCS in its least restrictive setting, allowing the highest level of wheel spin.

The page also includes a table showing the available Stability Settings for different Drive Modes:

- All-Purpose: On (default), Reduced, Off
- Sport: On (default), Reduced, Off
- Snow: On (default), Reduced, Off
- All-Terrain: On (default), Reduced, Off
- Soft Sand: Only Soft Sand (default) is available

1. Regenerative braking activates automatically when the driver lifts their foot off the accelerator pedal.

2. There are three settings for regenerative braking:

   - Standard: Moderate regenerative braking. This is the default setting for all modes except Snow and Soft Sand modes.
   
   - High: Stronger regenerative braking. The vehicle slows down faster and captures more energy.

This image shows a section from a vehicle manual titled "Driving" that focuses on "Ride Height" settings for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The information is presented in two tables:

1. The first table shows available ride heights based on different drive modes:
   - All-Purpose mode offers High, Standard (default), and Low settings
   - Sport mode offers Low (default) and Lowest settings
   - Snow mode offers High, Standard (default), and Low settings
   - All-Terrain mode offers Highest, High (default), and Standard settings
   - Soft Sand mode offers Highest, High, and Standard (default) settings

2. The second table provides specific measurements for ride height changes:
   - It shows the distance changes for two tire sizes: 33-in and 34-in diameter
   - Highest setting raises the vehicle by 3.54 in (90 mm) or 3.27 in (83 mm) respectively
   - High setting raises it by 1.57 in (40 mm) or 1.30 in (33 mm)
   - Standard is described as "Mid-level" for both tire sizes
   - Low setting lowers the vehicle by 1.38 in (35 mm) or 1.65 in (42 mm)
   - Lowest setting lowers it by 1.97 in (50 mm) or 2.24 in (57 mm)

The manual explains that ride height changes the distance from the lowest point of the vehicle to level ground. This information is likely crucial for off-road capabilities and adjusting the vehicle's performance in various driving conditions.

The content focuses on "Automatic Ride Height Changes" and provides information about the vehicle's adjustable suspension system. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Automatic Ride Height Changes:
   - Available in All-Purpose and Snow modes, except when towing a trailer
   - Automatically changes to Low ride height at higher speeds for efficiency
   - Returns to Standard ride height at lower speeds for ground clearance and comfort
   - Can be turned on/off or manually adjusted in All-Purpose or Snow mode

2. Notes:
   - Air suspension adjusts to maintain ride height while moving or stopped
   - Adjusts to keep the vehicle level when parked
   - Compressor may run for a few minutes after driving

3. Ride Height Details:
   - Cautions about using Low or Lowest ride heights in certain conditions
   - In All-Purpose or Snow mode with High ride height, vehicle lowers to Standard at speeds above 45 mph (72 km/h)
   - Off-Road modes with Highest ride height are limited to speeds under 20 mph (32 km/h)

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S model, focusing on the "Trailer Hitch" section. The page provides instructions for removing and reinstalling the trailer hitch cover. Here's a summary of the content:

1. The Rivian R1S has an integrated 2 in (5 cm) Class IV receiver and a 7-pin trailer connector behind the trailer hitch cover under the rear bumper.

2. To remove the trailer hitch cover:
   - Use a flathead screwdriver to loosen the screws in the cover (quarter-turn counterclockwise).
   - A caution note warns not to fully release the screws as they stay attached to the cover.
   - Grip the cover and pull it down vertically to remove it.

3. To reinstall the trailer hitch cover:
   - Align the cover tabs with the trailer hitch slot, ensuring the cover is vertical.
   - Raise the cover vertically to insert the tabs, then push it into the slot until flush with the bumper.

The page includes a simple diagram showing how to remove the cover with a screwdriver, indicated by a downward arrow.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically focusing on "Trailer Settings" for a Rivian R1S vehicle. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Trailer Settings:
   - Various drive modes are available for towing a trailer safely, including All-Purpose, Snow, All-Terrain, Soft Sand, and Rock Crawl (some modes are specific to certain motor configurations).
   - The manual emphasizes the importance of choosing the correct ride height when loading and towing a trailer.

2. Vehicle Features When Towing:
   - Maximum torque and trailer sway control are always on.
   - Certain features are disabled, including rear ultrasonic sensors, auto ride height, and some driver assistance features.
   - Manual Cruise Control remains available.

3. Trailer Profiles:
   - The vehicle can track trailer range impact, estimated weight, efficiency, and mileage for up to three trailers.
   - Users can edit trailer profiles in the Drive Modes > Trailers menu.

4. Trailer Learning:
   - The vehicle learns about the trailer's configuration and mass as you drive.
   - Learning occurs automatically and requires smooth acceleration on flat, straight roads.
   - It takes longer on curvy roads or at slower speeds.
   - A notification appears when learning is complete.

5. Start of Drive Detection:
   - The vehicle detects trailer mass and aerodynamics at the start of each drive and notifies of significant differences affecting range.

5. Two modes are described:
   - On: Engages at the posted speed limit when it's higher than the current vehicle speed.
   - Off: Engages with the current vehicle speed as the set speed.

7. Instructions for turning on and off the Manual Cruise Control are provided:
   - To turn on: Pull the drive stalk toward you and release.
   - To turn off: Push the drive stalk away from you and release, or press the brake pedal.

9. The feature disengages when applying the Manual Trailer Brake or if a trailer sway event occurs.

This image outlines the "Tread Lightly! Principles" for responsible driving, particularly in off-road or natural environments. The principles are presented with icons and brief explanations:

1. Travel Responsibly
   - Travel only in areas open to four-wheel drive vehicles.
   - Stay on the trail and avoid actions that may damage the trail.

2. Respect Rights of Others
   - Yield to hikers, bicyclists, and animals. Yield to those passing you or going uphill.
   - Respect private property.
   - Leave gates as you found them.

3. Educate Yourself
   - Plan for your trip.
   - Review maps and regulations.
   - Take a skills class.

4. Avoid Sensitive Areas
   - Drive over, not around, obstacles to avoid widening the trail.
   - Don't disturb historical artifacts, geographic features, and the natural environment.
   - Cross streams at designated fording points, where the road crosses the water.

5. Do Your Part
   - Leave the area better than you found it.
   - Haul out trash.
   - Minimize the use of fire. Observe fire restrictions.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page is titled "Driving" and focuses on instructions for driving in soft sand conditions. Here are the key points covered:

1. Soft Sand mode is available for Performance Dual-Motor and Quad-Motor models.

2. This mode optimizes systems like accelerator pedal response, torque distribution, and traction control for soft, dry sand and sand dunes.

3. Drivers should reduce tire pressures and refer to "Air Down Tires" for more information. Tires should be re-inflated to normal pressures before returning to roads and highways.

4. The manual advises using smooth and steady inputs for accelerator, brake, and steering, avoiding large and sudden changes.

5. It's important to maintain momentum and avoid stopping, staying afloat and being aware of shifting sand.

6. Turns and acceleration should be smooth and consistent, avoiding sudden moves or sharp turns.

7. If stopping is necessary, it's preferable to do so on a downhill, facing forward.

8. When starting from a stop, gradual accelerator pedal inputs should be used to avoid spinning the wheels and sinking them into the sand.

1. When closely following a vehicle or if a vehicle suddenly cuts in.

4. In busy urban or residential areas with rapidly changing conditions.

This page is from a vehicle user manual, specifically detailing the Adaptive Cruise Control (ACC) feature for a Rivian R1S vehicle. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Adaptive Cruise Control:
   - Maintains set speed and automatically adjusts to keep a safe distance from vehicles ahead.

2. Operating Conditions:
   - Not for off-road or towing use
   - Lane lines must be visible
   - Speed range: 20 to 85 mph (32 to 136 km/h)

3. Engaging ACC:
   - Pull drive stalk toward you and release
   - Vehicle chimes to confirm engagement
   - Set speed appears in a circle on the driver display

4. While ACC is engaged:
   - Press accelerator to temporarily exceed set speed
   - Release accelerator to resume ACC

5. Notes:
   - Regenerative braking occurs when disengaging ACC
   - ACC disengages if a door opens, seatbelt unbuckles, or shifting out of Drive
   - Vehicle can adjust ride height based on speed

6. Changing Speed and Following Distance:
   - Use controls on the right side of the steering wheel

This page is from a Rivian R1S vehicle manual, specifically detailing the "Driver Assistance" features. The page includes a diagram of what appears to be a steering wheel control and a table explaining the functions of different controls. Here's a breakdown of the information:

1. The diagram shows a thumb control with four numbered points.

2. The table explains the function of each numbered control:
   - Item 1: Thumb control up - Increases following distance
   - Item 2: Thumb control down - Decreases following distance
   - Item 3: Left thumb control button - Reduces speed
     • Quick press reduces by 1 mph (1 km/h) increments
     • Long press reduces to the nearest 5 mph (10 km/h) increments
   - Item 4: Right thumb control button - Increases speed
     • Quick press increases by 1 mph (1 km/h) increments
     • Long press increases to the nearest 5 mph (10 km/h) increments

3. Additional notes are provided:
   - The drive stalk can be used to set a new Adaptive Cruise Control or Highway Assist speed by accelerating to a new speed and pushing the drive stalk all the way down once and releasing.
   - If the "Speed Limit" option is selected in the Set Speed setting, pushing the drive stalk all the way down for 0.5 seconds and releasing will update the set speed to the posted speed limit when driving on a divided highway.

This page is from a vehicle user manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle, detailing the "Lane Change on Command" feature under the "Driver Assistance" section. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Lane Change on Command:
   - Automatically performs lane changes when requested while Highway Assist is engaged
   - May return the vehicle to the original lane if the change can't be completed due to road or traffic conditions

2. Operating Conditions:
   - Highway Assist must be engaged
   - Vehicle speed should be 50 to 85 mph (80 to 137 km/h)
   - Can also be used at 20 to 50 mph (32 to 80 km/h) if a vehicle is detected in the target lane

3. How to Engage:
   - Turn on the turn signal in the intended direction by pushing the lights stalk up or down to the second click

4. System Behavior:
   - Animations appear on the driver display to show lane change status
   - Turn signals automatically turn off after a successful lane change
   - Provides visual cues if the adjacent lane is blocked
   - The lane line flashes red and the vehicle chimes for a timeout after about 10 seconds
   - Warns if a requested lane change isn't supported (e.g., mandatory exit, merge lane)

5. Notes:
   - Turning the steering wheel disengages the system and switches to Adaptive Cruise Control
   - Changing turn signal direction during a lane change may affect the completion of the maneuver
---
The content focuses on cautionary information about the Lane Change on Command feature. Here are the key points outlined:

1. The system is designed to detect vehicles in adjacent lanes, but the driver is still responsible for visually checking that the target lane is clear before requesting a lane change.

2. Drivers should always monitor surrounding areas and be prepared to take control of the vehicle at any time.

3. There may be scenarios where the vehicle can neither complete the lane change nor return to the original lane.

4. The Lane Change on Command may not slow down the vehicle quickly enough if the vehicle in front brakes aggressively.

5. The system may perform erroneous lane changes if lane lines are not clearly visible. This can occur due to faded or missing lane lines, or when lanes are obstructed by cones, barrels, other objects, or debris.

The information is presented under a triangular caution symbol, emphasizing the importance of these safety warnings for the driver assistance feature.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically detailing the "Park Assist" feature under the "Driver Assistance" section. 
The Park Assist feature is described as a low-speed function that helps with reverse and parking maneuvers using ultrasonic sensors. These sensors measure distances around the vehicle and provide warnings through the driver display and audible alerts if objects are too close.

Key points from the manual include:

1. Sensor range: Up to 57 in (1.45 m) for front/rear, and up to 29 in (0.75 m) for sides.
2. Warning triggers in different driving modes (Park, Neutral, Drive, Reverse).
3. Visual and audible warnings for detected objects.
4. Chime frequency increases as objects get closer.
5. Warnings differ based on driving direction (forward vs. reverse).
6. The system is disabled when traveling less than 1 mph (1 km/h).
7. Opening doors or the tailgate affects the warning system.
8. Warnings stop after the vehicle is stationary for about 10 seconds.

The page is titled "Charging and Range" and focuses on the topic of "Low Battery". Here's a summary of the key information:

1. The manual advises charging the vehicle as soon as possible when the battery is low.

2. A table provides information on different battery status levels:
   - Battery low: Find a charger, choose Conserve mode if equipped. Battery icon turns yellow.
   - Battery very low: Same recommendation as above, but battery conditioning slows.
   - Battery almost empty: Charge the vehicle. Battery conditioning stops.

   - Charge immediately if battery is almost empty.

   - Extended time unplugged may permanently damage the battery.
   - Contact Rivian R1S if unable to charge.

4. Danger warning:
   - Never attempt to open or tamper with the vehicle battery. Contact Rivian R1S for battery service.

5. Keep unsupervised children away during charging.
6. Don't place fingers in the vehicle charge port.
7. Maximum operating temperature is 122°F (50°C).
8. Read all instructions before use.

The "Grounding Instructions" section explains the importance of proper grounding for the product to reduce the risk of electric shock. It mentions that the product comes with a grounding conductor and plug, which must be properly connected to a grounded outlet.

There's an additional warning, marked with a yellow warning triangle, about the risks of improper grounding. It advises consulting a qualified electrician if there are any doubts about proper grounding or if the plug doesn't fit the outlet.

   - Place it in the storage bag.

   - Can be activated by choosing "Save Clip" in the status bar or by honking the horn for more than a second

   - Chimes when recording starts or stops

   - Can be safely removed by choosing "Eject"

5. Incidents:
   - Enabled by default
   - Automatically records certain driving events like collisions or hard braking

6. Motion Cam:
   - Disabled by default
   - Can be turned on to record motion around the vehicle when away
   - Can record during alarm events
   - Has two modes: "Always on" and "Off at Home"

   - Users can navigate between events.
   - Options for play, pause, rewind, and forward are available.

   - Download: Copy video to external storage.
   - Star: Display video on Starred tab or save Motion Cam video from automatic deletion.
   - Delete: Remove one or all videos within an event.

5. Important Notes:
   - Deleting starred videos from Motion Cam or Alarm also deletes them from corresponding tabs.
   - Drive Cam clips are automatically saved to external storage and can't be copied.
   - Video deletion is permanent.

This page is from a user manual, specifically for a Rivian R1S vehicle, detailing instructions on "Storage and Security" and how to copy a video from the onboard hard drive to an external storage device. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. To copy a video, you need an external storage device (not included) with:
   - Minimum 128 GB storage (maximum 2 TB)
   - USB 3.x and USB 2.0 compatibility
   - Solid State Drive (SSD) recommended
   - Minimum 20 MB/s random write speed
   - FAT32 or MS-DOS (FAT) format

2. Steps to copy a video:
   1. Connect the external storage to a USB-C port in the center console
   2. Choose "Format Device" if prompted
   3. Select "Gear Guard" from the center display menu
   4. Select the event and video to download
   5. Choose "Download" to copy the video
   6. The vehicle saves the video to your external storage

3. To safely remove the device:
   - Choose "Gear Guard" from the menu
   - Select "Gear Guard Features"
   - Choose "Eject"

The document includes several notes, such as not using a USB hub or splitter, and that the vehicle may request to reformat the device if it doesn't detect a suitable format.

There's also a small illustration showing where to plug in the USB device in the vehicle's center console.

This page is from a user manual for a vehicle, specifically focusing on the "Storage and Security" section related to setting up and managing the Drive Cam feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Drive Cam: Records video in the background and events in real time.

2. Set Up the Drive Cam:
   - Requires an external storage device with:
     * Minimum 128 GB storage (maximum 2 TB)
     * USB 3.x and USB 2.0 compatibility
     * Solid State Drive (SSD) recommended
     * Minimum 20 MB/s random write speed
     * FAT32 or MS-DOS (FAT) format (Apple File System and NTFS not supported)

3. Initial setup process:
   1. Shift vehicle to Park
   2. Choose Gear Guard from the center display menu
   3. Choose Set Up Now and acknowledge terms
   4. Connect external storage to USB-C port in center console
   5. Follow on-screen instructions
   6. Format device if prompted
   7. Choose Done when setup is complete

4. Manage the Drive Cam:
   - Drive Cam Chime setting controls whether you hear a chime when recording starts or stops
   - Enabled by default when Drive Cam is on and storage is connected

   - Notify the SOS operator if there's an accidental call

This page focuses on"Storage and Security" features related to the vehicle's camera and recording systems. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Continuous Recordings:
   - The vehicle continuously records short video segments on an external storage device.
   - To access these recordings, users need to follow a 5-step process involving the Gear Guard feature and connecting the storage device to a computer.
   - If the storage device becomes full, the oldest recordings are automatically deleted.

2. Incidents Recording:
   - This feature is enabled by default and automatically records certain driving events like collisions or hard braking.
   - Users can enable or disable this feature through the Gear Guard menu.
   - Incident recordings start 15 seconds before the event and last for 2 minutes.
   - These videos are stored on the onboard hard drive and can be viewed in the Incidents video tab.

3. Important Notes:
   - Recording starts 15 seconds before initiating a Drive Cam clip.
   - The system notifies users when storage devices are full or close to full.
   - There's no guarantee that all relevant images for an incident will be captured.
   - The onboard hard drive may require management if it becomes full.
   - Vehicle Shipping mode disables the Incidents feature.

4. Storage Management:
   - Both external storage (for continuous recordings) and onboard storage (for incidents) have mechanisms to manage space when full or nearly full.

The page is titled "Storage and Security" and provides detailed information about the vehicle's alarm system. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Arm or Disarm the Alarm:
   - The alarm arms automatically when certain conditions are met, such as enabling the alarm, locking all doors, and no detection of people or authorized devices inside.

2. Alarm Triggers:
   - When armed, the alarm is triggered by an opened door, detected motion inside (if equipped), or if the vehicle tilts.

3. Panic Mode:
   - Pressing the Lock button on the key fob for 2 seconds activates panic mode.

4. Stop the Alarm:
   - When triggered, the vehicle flashes lights, sounds the horn, and sends a message to the Rivian R1S mobile app.
   - To stop the alarm, you can unlock the vehicle, lock it again, or let it time out after 30 seconds.

5. Additional Notes:
   - The alarm turns off after 5 minutes if repeatedly triggered, but reactivates when the immobilizer is turned off.
   - The vehicle's immobilizer helps prevent theft by preventing the vehicle from being driven when active.

This manual page provides comprehensive instructions for operating and understanding the security features of the Rivian R1S vehicle, particularly its alarm system.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S Camp Speaker, which is an accessory for a Rivian R1S vehicle. The page includes detailed speaker specifications and getting started instructions. Here's a breakdown of the key information:

Speaker Specifications:
- Model: RCS 1.0
- Dimensions: 9.9 in x 6.7 in x 5.1 in (252 mm x 170 mm x 128.5 mm)
- Weight: 5.7 lb (2.6 kg)
- Battery capacity: 32 Watt hours
- Charge time: 3 hours maximum
- Play time: 6.5 hours minimum (audio only)
- Lantern (60% brightness): 3.5 hours
- Input power: 30 Watts
- Input rating: Type C: DC 5 V / 9 V / 15 V / 20 V, Pogo pin: DC 12 V
- Output rating: Type C: DC 5 V / 2 A
- Operating temperature: 32 to 104°F (0 to 40°C)
- Safe storage temperature: Up to 185°F (85°C)

Getting Started:
The manual instructs users to locate the speaker in the Accessory Dock of the center console if their vehicle is equipped with it.

Important Note:
The speaker needs to be fully charged before initial use. Users are instructed to undock the speaker and plug it into a power source using a USB-C cable with power delivery similar to a laptop charger for faster charging. The charge level can be checked by pressing the Lantern button twice.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically focusing on the "Accessories" section and detailing information about the battery and charging of a speaker system. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Battery:
   - Checking Charge Level: Press the Lantern button twice on the speaker.
   - Green light indicates 75% to 100% charge
   - Amber light indicates 35% to 74% charge
   - Red light indicates 0% to 34% charge

2. Charging the Speaker:
   - Automatically charges when docked and the vehicle is driving
   - Can be charged via USB-C when undocked
   - LED light above USB-C connector indicates charging status
   - Fully charged when LED shows solid white
   - Warning tone plays at 5% battery remaining
   - Speaker powers down if not charged

3. Note on Temperature:
   - Normal operation requires battery temperature between 32°F to 104°F (0 to 40°C)

4. Charging with USB-C Cable:
   - Use when speaker is not docked
   - Recommended to use a laptop-style charger for faster charging
   - Charging time varies from 3 hours (with power delivery) to 12 hours (without power delivery)

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S product, specifically focusing on safety information for accessories, likely a speaker system. Here are the key points:

1. Important Safety Information:
   - DANGER: The rechargeable battery may explode if incorrectly replaced. Contact Rivian R1S for battery replacement.
   - The speaker forces a shutdown to protect the battery if the temperature falls outside the range of -4 to +140°F (-20 to +60°C).

2. General Safety Instructions:
   - Read and keep instructions
   - Heed all warnings
   - Clean only with a soft dry cloth
   - Don't block ventilation openings
   - Don't install near heat sources
   - Avoid leaving the speaker in direct sunlight or excessive heat

3. CAUTION:
   - Temperatures exceeding 185°F (85°C) can damage the speaker

4. Additional Safety Precautions:
   - Don't expose to heavy rainstorms
   - The lantern light flashes red to indicate overheating or overcooling
   - Use only manufacturer-specified accessories
   - Properly manage cables to prevent tripping hazards
   - Unplug during lightning storms or long periods of disuse
   - Refer service to qualified personnel, especially if damaged

The document emphasizes the importance of proper handling, temperature management, and authorized servicing to ensure safe operation of the device.

The warnings listed are:

1. Remove the tent and crossbars before going through an automated car wash.
2. Do not use fuel-burning or oxygen-consuming devices inside the tent, including candles, gas lanterns, kerosene lamps, stoves, and cooking/heating appliances.
3. Do not set up the tent near a campfire or any other flame source.
4. Inspect the mounting hardware before driving the vehicle.

6. Do not drill additional holes in the ladder.
7. When using the Three-Person Tent, ensure the ladder angle is between 75° and 90°.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically detailing how to lock the crossbars on the vehicle's roof rack. The page is titled "Accessories" and provides instructions for "Lock the Crossbars" in three steps:

1. Lock the crossbars with the key by turning clockwise.
2. Push the crossbar paddle all the way down to cover the lock cylinder.
3. Repeat steps 1 and 2 on the remaining crossbar ends to ensure the crossbars are fully locked.

The instructions are accompanied by two diagrams illustrating the locking process.

Below the instructions, there's a warning section that includes three important points:

- Secure crossbars and loads before and after driving, especially when traveling through rough terrain, as loose crossbars and unsecured loads could cause a serious crash.
- Don't drill holes in the crossbars. Only use manufacturer recommended parts and accessories.
- Modifications or accessories not provided by the manufacturer will void the manufacturer's warranty. The owner assumes liability for any damage or crashes caused by unauthorized modifications.

This page focuses on"Crossbar Loading" under the Accessories section. The page contains important safety information and specifications for loading cargo on the vehicle's crossbars. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. WARNING:
   - Don't exceed the maximum specified load for the Cargo Crossbars.
   - Be aware of overall vehicle payload capacities when loading.
   - Refer to the Tire and Loading Information label and Load Carrying Capacity Modification label on the driver's door pillar for maximum allowable vehicle payload.

2. Load Specifications:
   - Maximum dynamic (driving) load: 250 lbs (113 kg) per crossbar pair.
   - Maximum static (parked) load: 780 lbs (353 kg) per crossbar pair, e.g., for a rooftop tent when parked at a campsite.

3. Loading Instructions:
   - Evenly distribute the load on the crossbars.
   - Maintain a low center of gravity for the load.

4. DANGER:
   - Any load extending over the windshield must be secured to both the front and rear of the vehicle, in addition to the Cargo Crossbars.
   - Failure to properly secure loads can result in property damage, personal injury, or death.

This page is detailing the "Service and Maintenance" section, focusing on "Exterior Cleaning" and the "Car Wash Mode" feature.

The document explains that Car Wash Mode can be activated through Quick Controls on the center display. When activated, it performs several functions to protect the vehicle during a car wash:

1. Rolls up all windows
2. Closes the door handles
3. Closes the charge port door if not charging
4. Mutes parking sensor alert chimes
5. Prevents automatic windshield wipers from activating
6. Suppresses automatic switching between Day and Night themes
7. Suppresses proximity lock and unlock

There are additional notes explaining how to open doors when in Car Wash Mode, along with an illustration showing how to push on the indent of the door handle to open it if the handles aren't presenting.

An important note at the bottom states that the vehicle speed must be below 12 mph (19 km/h) to enable Car Wash Mode, and that this mode defaults to "off" after a vehicle restart.

This page focuses onthe "Commercial Car Wash" section under "Service and Maintenance". Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Standard car wash services can be used to clean the vehicle.
2. Ensure all windows are up and side mirrors are folded before entering the car wash.
3. Lock the vehicle to prevent the charge port door from opening if Car Wash mode isn't turned on.
4. For "touchless" car washes, put the vehicle in Park.
5. For car washes requiring driving on a rail:
   - Turn on Car Wash mode from Park position.
   - Put the vehicle in Neutral using the drive stalk or on-screen button.

Important notes:
- If Vehicle Hold engages while in Neutral, press the brake pedal to release Hold.
- When Car Wash mode is on and the vehicle is in Neutral, it will stay in Neutral even if you leave the driver's seat.
- Only use Car Wash mode on flat ground to prevent rolling.

The document also includes a caution symbol and box, emphasizing the importance of being cautious when using Car Wash mode in Neutral.

This page is from a service and maintenance manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically focusing on hand washing and waxing the vehicle. Here are the key points:

1. Hand Wash and Wax:
   - Wash the vehicle before excessive dirt builds up
   - Roll up windows and close/lock doors
   - Don't use hot water or wash in direct sunlight

2. Caution:
   - Don't use water repellent products on the windshield as they can affect rain detection and automatic wiper function

3. Hand Wash Danger:
   - Ensure the vehicle is not charging when washing to avoid electrocution risk
   - Avoid spraying water on electronics or exposed cabling

4. Note:
   - Users can configure a Car Wash mode in the Rivian R1S mobile app
   - Turning off Bluetooth can prevent handles and charge port door from opening mid-wash

5. Washing technique:
   - Use a hose or standard pressure washer
   - Use a side-to-side sweeping motion
   - Avoid prolonged concentrated pressure on a single area

This page is from a vehicle service and maintenance manual, specifically focusing on interior cleaning. The page is titled "Interior Cleaning" under the "Service and Maintenance" section. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Caution:
   - Don't use harsh cleaners like bleach, ammonia, or silicone.
   - Avoid cleaners with wax or petroleum.
   - Don't remove the AC/DC inverter cover when cleaning under the front passenger seat.

2. General cleaning instructions:
   - Clean the interior periodically.
   - Remove trash and debris.
   - Remove and vacuum floor mats, floors, and seats.
   - Clean mirrors, windows, and windshield with appropriate methods.
   - Wipe seats, surfaces, and speaker grills with a damp cloth.
   - Turn off climate controls when cleaning around vents and dashboard.

3. Note:
   - Lightly dampen cleaning cloths; don't oversaturate.
   - Don't spray cleaner directly on surfaces or soak cloths in cleaning solution.

This page is from a vehicle service and maintenance manual, specifically focusing on windshield washer fluid. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Seasonality and Temperature Rating:
   - Use fluid rated for the season and temperature range where the vehicle is located.
   - Dilute concentrated formulas as needed.
   - Always refer to temperature ratings and instructions on the fluid bottle.

2. Important Notes on Fluid Ratings:
   - Cold weather-rated fluid performs best in colder temperatures but is unnecessary in milder weather.
   - Milder temperature fluids contain lower levels of volatile organic compounds (VOCs).
   - Using the wrong type of fluid can release excess VOCs, contributing to ozone and smog.

3. Refill Warnings:
   - DANGER: Concentrated fluid is highly flammable and may ignite if exposed to heat.
   - WARNING: Vehicle components may be hot after driving. Ensure areas are cool before touching or pouring fluid.

4. Important Dilution Instructions:
   - Some fluids must be diluted. Follow manufacturer's instructions.
   - Dilute in a separate container, not in the vehicle reservoir.

5. Refill Steps:
   1. Park on a level surface with the vehicle off.
   2. Open the hood and locate the reservoir cap.
   3. Pry up the cap to access the opening.
   4. Pour in fluid until the foam float rises or the reservoir is full.
   5. Replace and secure the cap.
---
This page is from a vehicle service and maintenance manual, specifically detailing the process for wiper blade replacement. The manual appears to be for a Rivian R1S vehicle, as indicated by the Rivian R1S logo at the bottom of the page.

The document is divided into two main sections: Front Wiper Blades and Rear Wiper Blade.

For the Front Wiper Blades, it provides a 6-step process:
1. Choose Mirrors and Wipers from the center display.
2. Switch wiper mode to Off, and ensure the vehicle is in Park.
3. Enable Wiper Service mode to move the wipers out of the wiper park position.
4. Bend the wiper arms at the hinge as needed.
5. Remove and replace the wiper blades. Set the new blades on the windshield.
6. Disable Wiper Service mode from the center display to return the wipers to the park position.

There's a WARNING note about positioning both wiper blades on the windshield before exiting Wiper Service mode to prevent damage to the vehicle's hood.

A NOTE also mentions to use a j-hook hybrid wiper blade.

A table is included showing the Wiper Location and Wiper Size:
- Front driver's side: 24 in (600 mm)
- Front passenger's side: 18 in (450 mm)

For the Rear Wiper Blade, it provides a 4-step process:
1. Choose Mirrors and Wipers from the center display.
2. Switch wiper mode to Off, and ensure the vehicle is in Park.
3. Enable Wiper Service mode.
4. Pull the wiper away from the rear window about 15 degrees.

This page is from a service and maintenance manual for Rivian R1S vehicles, specifically focusing on tire rotation. Here are the key points:

1. Tire Rotation:
   - Rivian R1S recommends rotating tires every 7,500 mi (12,000 km) to ensure even tread wear and extend tire life.
   - A four-tire rotation is recommended to ensure the spare tire (if equipped) is in excellent condition.

2. Rotation Pattern:
   1. Move the rear tires to the same sides on the front.
   2. Move the front tires to the opposite sides on the rear.

This page is from a vehicle service and maintenance manual, specifically focusing on tire replacement. Here are the key points covered:

1. Tire Replacement:
   - Replace tires when worn for safety and maximum performance.
   - Worn tires increase accident risk in reduced traction conditions like rain or snow.

2. Tread Wear:
   - Tire wear reduces tread depth.
   - The vehicle's tires have tread wear indicators at 2/32 in (1.6 mm).
   - An illustration shows a tire with wear indicators.

3. Tire Inspection:
   - Regularly inspect tires and replace before tread wear indicators appear as a solid line.
   - Another illustration shows a tire with visible wear indicators.

4. Tire Maintenance:
   - Keep tires properly inflated for even wear and maximum traction.
   - Rotate tires every 7,500 mi (12,000 km) for even wear and extended life.

5. Important Note:
   - Rivian R1S recommends that the tread depth difference between left and right tires on each axle not exceed 2/32 in (1.6 mm).
   - If the difference exceeds this, both tires on the same axle may need replacement.
   - Follow local regulations for tread wear limits.

The page provides detailed instructions for changing a tire and storing the removed wheel. Here are the key points:

1. Tire inflation: The compact spare tire should be inflated to 61 psi (420 kPa).

2. Safety warning: Keep hands and fingers away from the tire during inflation or deflation to avoid pinch hazards.

3. Tire changing process:
   - Lower the jack until the tire touches the ground but doesn't bear full vehicle weight.
   - Torque the lug nuts in an alternating star pattern to 190 Nm.
   - If no torque tool is available, tighten until the lug nuts can't be turned further.
   - The lug nuts are M14 x 1.5.

4. Illustrations show:
   - The star pattern for tightening lug nuts
   - A lug wrench
   - A diagram of the wheel and lug nuts

5. Final steps:
   - Lower the vehicle completely
   - Remove the tire service kit and wheel chocks
   - For full-size spare, swap the center cap from the removed wheel

6. Storing the removed wheel:
   - Access vehicle settings in the center display
   - Turn off Tire Change mode
   - Lower the vehicle for better access to the spare tire compartment
   - Set the ride height to Standard under All-Purpose drive mode

7. Safety note: Ensure the area beneath the vehicle is clear before lowering.

3. Warning: Advises against servicing the vehicle on uneven or soft terrain, narrow shoulders, or near oncoming traffic.

4. Caution: 
   - Use Rivian R1S-supplied tire sealant kit for emergencies only
   - Tire sealant only repairs holes in tire tread, not exceeding 0.25 in (6 mm) in diameter

5. Onboard Air Compressor and Tire Sealant Kit instructions:
   1. Park the vehicle in a safe, level location
   2. Turn on hazard lights
   3. Locate the tire sealant kit in the front trunk
   4. Remove the tire valve stem cap
   5. Remove the valve core using the provided tool
   6. Deflate the tire
   7. Attach the sealant hose to the valve stem
   8. Insert the nozzle into the sealant hose
   9. Squeeze the sealant into the tire
   10. Remove the sealant pouch and hose
   11. Reinstall the valve core
   12. Reinflate the tire using the air compressor

The page is titled "Troubleshooting and Help" and focuses on how to "Jump-Start the 12 V System". Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Signs of a discharged 12 V system include:
   - Doors and storage areas not unlocking
   - Vehicle not responding to key fob
   - Lighting not illuminating
   - Displays not turning on

2. A 12 V system jump start provides power to:
   - Open doors and front trunk
   - Open charge port door
   - Release electronic park brake

3. For 2025 model year vehicles, it also powers:
   - Adjusting front seats
   - Opening/closing front windows
   - Accessing all storage areas

4. Important notes after a jump start:
   - If you can open doors but can't shift to Drive, plug into a nearby charger
   - If you can open doors and shift to Drive, you can plug in or drive to a charger
   - If doors won't open, contact Rivian R1S for transport
   - If the high-voltage battery is at zero charge and can't be charged, contact Rivian R1S for transport

The document provides detailed instructions for various scenarios and emphasizes contacting Rivian R1S support when certain issues arise. This manual page is designed to help Rivian R1S owners troubleshoot basic electrical system problems and understand when professional assistance is needed.

The page is titled "Troubleshooting and Help" and focuses on how to jump-start the 12V system of the vehicle. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Safety Warnings:
   - DANGER: Never allow jump cables to touch each other or any metal part of the vehicle.
   - CAUTION: Don't use a Rivian R1S vehicle to jump-start another vehicle.

2. Prerequisites:
   - Ensure an adequate external power source is available.
   - If using a tow truck, it must run until the Rivian R1S vehicle powers up.
   - If using a portable jump starter, it must maintain 13-16V at 30A.

3. Jump-Start Procedure:
   1. Remove the trailer hitch cover to access the jump-start wire harness.
   2. Remove the round jump port cover to the right of the trailer hitch.
   3. Pull out the jump-start wire harness and remove protective tape from connectors.
   4. Connect the red positive lead (+) from the external power source to the red lead on the jump-start wire harness.
   5. Connect the black negative lead (-) from the external power source to the black lead on the jump-start wire harness.

4. After Jump-Starting:
   - When the 12V system has enough power, you can unlock the vehicle to open doors, front trunk, and charge port door.
   - On 2025 model year vehicles, additional functions become available, such as adjusting front seats, operating windows, and accessing storage areas.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically the "Troubleshooting and Help" section focusing on the Emergency SOS feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Emergency SOS:
   - Use the SOS button on the overhead console in emergencies.
   - It connects to a 24/7 national call center for assessment and dispatching help.
   - The vehicle can automatically initiate an SOS call if it detects a significant collision.
   - The system suppresses background noise and displays your location during the call.

2. Additional Information:
   - The feature works in cellular coverage areas, even without your phone.
   - For non-emergency assistance, contact Rivian R1S.
   - Data collection during SOS calls is addressed in the Data and Privacy section.

3. Notes:
   - Instructions for retrying the call if the center can't be reached.
   - Pressing SOS during a phone call disconnects that call.
   - Accidental calls can be canceled within 20 seconds.
   - After 20 seconds, the call is automatically placed if not confirmed or canceled.
   - SOS options aren't visible when the vehicle is in Reverse.
   - The SOS button doesn't work outside the United States or Canada.

4. Hazard Lights:
   - In emergencies or malfunctions, press the Hazard Lights button on the overhead console to alert surrounding vehicles.

This page is from a vehicle manual, specifically discussing the Event Data Recorder (EDR) feature. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. The vehicle is equipped with an EDR to record data in certain crash or near crash-like situations.

2. The EDR records data for about 30 seconds or less, including:
   - How various vehicle systems were operating
   - Whether safety belts were buckled
   - How far the driver was pressing the accelerator/brake pedal
   - How fast the vehicle was traveling

3. This data helps understand the circumstances of crashes and injuries.

4. Important note: 
   - EDR only records data in non-trivial crash situations
   - No data is recorded under normal driving conditions
   - No personal data (name, gender, age, crash location) is recorded
   - However, law enforcement could combine EDR data with other personally identifying information during an investigation

5. Special equipment and access to the vehicle/EDR is required to read the data.

6. Besides the vehicle manufacturer, other parties like law enforcement with special equipment can access this data if they have access to the vehicle or EDR.

This page is from what appears to be a user manual or privacy policy document for Rivian R1S vehicles. The page is titled "Legal and Reference" and focuses on "Data and Privacy" policies. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Data and Privacy:
   - Rivian R1S values customer privacy and directs users to their Data Privacy Notice for more information.
   - Users can contact Rivian R1S with questions about vehicle features or functionality.
   - Data is central to many features in Rivian R1S's connected driving experience.
   - Users can adjust privacy settings through the vehicle's center display.

2. Exterior Cameras:
   - Rivian R1S uses shared exterior camera images for driver assistance improvement.
   - Users can opt out of sharing these images.
   - Privacy-enhancing techniques are applied, including:
     - Images are not associated with specific vehicles (except in crashes)
     - Faces and license plates are blurred
     - First and last three minutes of drives are not used
     - Precise location data is only attached when agreed to by the user

3. Interior Camera:
   - Located in the rearview mirror, off by default
   - When enabled, it's used for safety systems and driver monitoring
   - Images are occasionally captured based on specific triggers
   - Privacy measures are in place to protect user data

4. Location Data Sharing:
   - Precise location data (within about a half-mile radius) is shared for certain features
   - Rivian R1S does not sell personal data

The document emphasizes Rivian R1S's commitment to user privacy while balancing the need for data to improve vehicle features and safety systems. It provides users with information on how their data is used and what control they have over its collection and sharing.

This page is from a user manual for a Rivian R1S vehicle, specifically detailing the "Clear Settings" function. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. Clear Settings Purpose:
   - Removes personal information and preferences from the vehicle
   - Resets certain system functions and services to default

2. What Clear Settings removes:
   - Saved locations, favorites, radio stations, stored Gear Guard videos
   - Paired garages, Bluetooth devices, synced contacts or media
   - Hotspots, language and units, audio settings
   - Spotify and Alexa connections (may need additional online steps)

3. Important Notes:
   - Doesn't remove driver profiles or paired keys
   - Doesn't delete information stored on the Rivian R1S cloud
   - The action cannot be undone
   - For selling a Rivian R1S, visit Rivian R1S.com/resale-help

4. Important Considerations:
   - Park in a safe place with internet connection
   - Process takes a few minutes; display goes dark and vehicle reboots
   - If selling, additional steps with Rivian R1S are required

5. How to Use Clear Settings:
   1. Go to Settings > Vehicle > Service > Clear Settings
   2. Choose "Learn More" for a summary and QR code for full instructions
   3. Select "Clear Settings" at the bottom of the Learn More page, then "Clear Now"

This image contains important information about reporting safety defects for vehicles in the United States. Here's a summary of the key points:

1. The document is titled "Reporting Safety Defects in the United States" and appears to be part of a legal and reference section, likely from a vehicle manual.

2. It instructs that if you believe your vehicle has a defect that could cause a crash, injury, or death, you should immediately inform the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA) in addition to notifying Rivian R1S.

3. The NHTSA may open an investigation if it receives similar complaints and may order a recall and remedy campaign if a safety defect is found. However, NHTSA cannot become involved in individual problems between you, your dealer, or Rivian R1S.
